# ZAFTO HOME â€” Property Intelligence Platform
## Product Specification v0.1 | February 2026
## Tereda Software LLC â€” CONFIDENTIAL

---

# THE IDEA IN ONE SENTENCE

Every homeowner gets a permanent, portable property record that builds itself through contractor work â€” free forever, with premium AI features that turn ZAFTO into the operating system for home ownership.

---

# WHY THIS EXISTS

Right now, homeowners have no single source of truth for their property. Service records live in contractor CRMs. Warranties are in email. Equipment specs are in kitchen drawers. Permits are at city hall. When a homeowner switches contractors, moves, or sells â€” all of that context evaporates.

ZAFTO already captures this data on the contractor side. The CRM tracks every job, every piece of equipment installed, every invoice, every inspection. The Client Portal already surfaces this to homeowners. The leap is small but the implications are massive: **let the homeowner own that data permanently.**

---

# THE CONTRACTOR TENSION

This is the single biggest risk to the business. ZAFTO's current revenue comes from contractors. If homeowners can "shop around," contractors may see ZAFTO as a threat instead of a tool. Get this wrong and you lose your existing customer base. Get it right and you've built something 10x bigger.

## The Fear
"If my client can take their record and shop around, I'm training my competitor."

## The Reality
- **95% of homeowner-contractor switches happen because of bad experiences, not because shopping was easy.** Making it easier to compare doesn't create disloyalty â€” bad work creates disloyalty.
- **Transparency favors the best contractors.** If you do great work, your 10-year service history with a client is the most powerful sales tool imaginable. No competitor can match that trust.
- **The data already belongs to the homeowner.** They paid for the work. They own the equipment. Locking data in a CRM doesn't prevent switching â€” it just makes ZAFTO look like it's hiding something.

## The Solution: Contractor Advantage Program

Design the system so being on ZAFTO makes the contractor's position STRONGER, not weaker.

### 1. Preferred Contractor Status
When a contractor does work through ZAFTO, they automatically become the homeowner's **Preferred Contractor** for that trade. This means:

- The homeowner's AI recommends THEM first for related work
- They appear at the top of any quote comparison
- They get a "Trusted by this homeowner since 20XX" badge
- They get first-right-of-refusal on new service requests (24hr head start before the request goes to the marketplace)

**The contractor earns this by doing work. They lose it by losing the client.** This is a moat that rewards loyalty.

### 2. Contractor Intelligence Feed
Contractors on ZAFTO get insights no one else has:

- "3 of your clients have water heaters approaching end-of-life"
- "Sarah Johnson's HVAC warranty expires in 60 days â€” schedule a maintenance visit?"
- "Mike Chen's panel upgrade is 2 years old â€” time for a follow-up inspection"

**This is proactive revenue generation.** The contractor who stays on ZAFTO sees the opportunities. The one who leaves is flying blind.

### 3. Reputation Compounds
Every completed job, every positive review, every on-time arrival, every warranty honored â€” it all accumulates in the contractor's ZAFTO profile. This reputation is visible to homeowners shopping for new contractors. A contractor with 200 verified jobs and a 4.9 rating doesn't fear transparency. They weaponize it.

### 4. The "Switching Tax" Works Both Ways
Yes, a homeowner can take their record to a new contractor. But the new contractor has to be on ZAFTO to see it. This means:
- More contractors join the platform (network effect)
- The switching homeowner is still inside ZAFTO's ecosystem
- ZAFTO earns from both sides of the transaction

### 5. What Contractors Should Actually Fear
Not Home Portal â€” but the alternative. If ZAFTO doesn't build this, someone else will. And that someone won't have the contractor's interests in mind at all. Better for contractors that this platform is built BY a company that already serves them.

---

# PRODUCT TIERS

## Free Tier â€” "Your Home's Memory" (Forever Free)

The free tier must be genuinely useful, not a teaser. It's the hook that gets millions of homeowners onto the platform.

### Core Features
- **Property Profile**: Address, sq footage, year built, systems overview
- **Equipment Passport**: Every piece of major equipment with make, model, serial, install date, installer, warranty status
- **Service History Timeline**: Chronological record of all work done, by whom, with what materials
- **Document Vault**: Estimates, invoices, permits, inspection reports, warranties, photos â€” all in one place
- **Warranty Tracker**: Expiration alerts, coverage details, claim instructions
- **Lifespan Intelligence**: "Your water heater is 8 years old. Average lifespan: 10-12 years." (Based on equipment data, not AI â€” this is just math)
- **Maintenance Calendar**: Recommended maintenance schedule based on installed equipment
- **Contractor Ratings**: Rate and review contractors who've done work

### How It Populates
- **Automatic** from any ZAFTO-connected contractor (the killer feature â€” zero effort)
- **Manual entry** by homeowner (for work done before ZAFTO or by non-ZAFTO contractors)
- **Receipt/invoice scanning** via camera (OCR extracts equipment details)
- **Import from other platforms** (HomeAdvisor, Angi, etc. â€” if possible)

### Why Free Works
The free tier creates the network. Every homeowner on the platform is a potential lead for contractors. The more homeowners, the more valuable ZAFTO is to contractors. The more contractors, the more automatic data flows to homeowners. Flywheel.

---

## Premium Tier â€” "Home Intelligence" ($7.99/month or $79/year)

### AI Property Advisor
The AI knows your specific property â€” not generic advice, but recommendations based on YOUR equipment, YOUR service history, YOUR climate zone, YOUR energy costs.

- **"Should I replace or repair?"** â€” AI analyzes equipment age, repair history, energy efficiency, and current market prices to give a specific recommendation with dollar math
- **"Is this quote fair?"** â€” Upload a quote, AI compares against regional averages, material costs, and complexity. "This $14K HVAC quote is 8% above average for your area, but includes a variable-speed system that will save ~$400/year in energy"
- **"What upgrades make sense?"** â€” Based on equipment age, energy data, and available rebates. "A heat pump conversion would cost ~$12K but you qualify for a $2K federal rebate and $1,500 state rebate. Payback period: 4.2 years"
- **"What's my home's maintenance debt?"** â€” Aggregate view of deferred maintenance with cost projections. "You have $8,200 in recommended maintenance. Deferring the roof repair another 2 years increases risk of interior water damage ($15-40K)"

### Smart Alerts
- Equipment recall notifications (pulled from CPSC database)
- Warranty expiration warnings with renewal options
- Seasonal maintenance reminders customized to your equipment
- Energy rate changes that affect upgrade ROI calculations
- Building code changes that affect your property

### Quote Marketplace
- Request quotes from multiple ZAFTO contractors simultaneously
- Side-by-side comparison with AI analysis
- Preferred contractor gets 24hr first look
- Transparent pricing powered by ZAFTO's price book data across thousands of contractors
- "Your preferred contractor's quote of $8,400 is 5% below the average of 3 quotes received"

### Home Health Score (Premium Detail)
- Free tier shows the number (92%)
- Premium shows the breakdown: what's driving it down, what to prioritize, projected score in 1/3/5 years
- "Your score dropped 3 points because your HVAC filter hasn't been replaced in 6 months"

### Property Value Intelligence
- How maintenance and upgrades affect estimated property value
- "The kitchen remodel added an estimated $18K to your home value"
- "Deferred roof maintenance is reducing your value by an estimated $5K"
- Integration with public property data where available

### Multi-Property Support
- Manage rental properties, vacation homes, parents' house
- Separate equipment records and contractor relationships per property
- Consolidated dashboard across all properties

---

## Contractor Marketplace â€” Revenue Model

### For Homeowners (Free)
- Request service through the platform
- Preferred contractor gets first look (24hrs)
- If preferred declines or homeowner wants options â†’ opens to marketplace
- Side-by-side quote comparison with AI analysis

### For Contractors â€” Lead Generation
- **Free ZAFTO CRM subscribers**: Get organic leads from their existing clients (this is already built into the Client Portal)
- **Paid ZAFTO CRM subscribers**: Get marketplace leads in their service area
- **Lead pricing**: Pay-per-qualified-lead or monthly subscription for unlimited leads in a zone
- **Featured placement**: Higher visibility in quote comparisons (like Google Ads for home services)

### Revenue Streams
| Stream | Model | Est. Revenue Per Unit |
|--------|-------|----------------------|
| Homeowner Premium | $7.99/mo subscription | $96/year per homeowner |
| Contractor CRM | Existing subscription | $99-299/mo |
| Marketplace Leads | Per-lead or subscription | $25-75/lead |
| Featured Placement | Monthly fee | $199-499/mo per contractor |
| Transaction Fee | % of invoices paid through ZAFTO | 2.5-3% |

---

# DATA OWNERSHIP & PORTABILITY

This is non-negotiable and should be a core brand promise.

## Homeowner's Data Rights
- **Full export anytime**: One-click download of entire property record (PDF + structured data)
- **API access** (premium): Connect to other platforms, insurance, real estate
- **Delete anytime**: Full GDPR-style data deletion
- **Survives contractor relationship**: If your contractor leaves ZAFTO or goes out of business, your data stays
- **Transfers with property sale**: Option to transfer record to new homeowner (massive selling point for real estate)

## Contractor's Data Rights
- Contractors own their business data (CRM, pricing, internal notes)
- Contractors do NOT own the homeowner's property record
- Service records are shared: contractor sees their work history with the client, homeowner sees all work history
- Contractor's proprietary pricing/margins are never exposed to homeowners

## The Line
- **Homeowner sees**: What was done, when, by whom, what it cost them, what equipment was installed
- **Homeowner doesn't see**: Contractor's material costs, margins, internal notes, team communications
- **Contractor sees**: Their work history with the client, equipment they installed, AI-generated opportunities
- **Contractor doesn't see**: Other contractors' quotes (unless the homeowner explicitly shares for price-match)

---

# TECHNICAL ARCHITECTURE

## Data Flow

```
ZAFTO CRM (Contractor)
    â”‚
    â”œâ”€â”€ Job completed â†’ auto-creates/updates property record
    â”œâ”€â”€ Equipment installed â†’ adds to Equipment Passport
    â”œâ”€â”€ Invoice paid â†’ adds to payment history
    â”œâ”€â”€ Document uploaded â†’ adds to Document Vault
    â”‚
    â–¼
ZAFTO HOME (Homeowner's permanent record)
    â”‚
    â”œâ”€â”€ Firestore: Property data, equipment, service history
    â”œâ”€â”€ Cloud Storage: Documents, photos, receipts
    â”œâ”€â”€ Claude API: AI advisor (premium)
    â”‚
    â–¼
ZAFTO MARKETPLACE (Connects both sides)
    â”œâ”€â”€ Service requests flow from homeowner â†’ preferred contractor â†’ marketplace
    â”œâ”€â”€ Quotes flow from contractors â†’ homeowner with AI analysis
    â””â”€â”€ Payments processed through ZAFTO (transaction fee)
```

## Database Schema (Additions to Existing)

### Properties Collection (Expanded)
```
properties/{propertyId}
  ownerId: string (homeowner's auth ID â€” THIS is the key change)
  address: { street, city, state, zip, coordinates }
  details: { type, sqft, yearBuilt, bedrooms, bathrooms, stories, lotSize }
  healthScore: number (computed)
  preferredContractors: { [trade]: contractorId }
  tier: 'free' | 'premium'
  createdAt, updatedAt
```

### Equipment Collection (Expanded)
```
properties/{propertyId}/equipment/{equipmentId}
  category: 'hvac' | 'electrical' | 'plumbing' | 'roofing' | 'appliance'
  name, make, model, serialNumber
  installDate, installedBy: { contractorId, contractorName }
  warranty: { type, provider, expirationDate, coverage }
  lifespan: { averageYears, condition, lastServiced }
  recalls: [{ recallId, description, severity, date }]
  status: 'healthy' | 'maintenance_due' | 'attention' | 'critical' | 'end_of_life'
```

### Service History (New â€” Owned by Property, Not Contractor)
```
properties/{propertyId}/serviceHistory/{recordId}
  contractorId, contractorName, contractorRating
  trade: string
  type: 'installation' | 'repair' | 'maintenance' | 'inspection' | 'emergency'
  description, date, cost
  equipmentAffected: [equipmentId]
  documents: [{ type, url, name }]
  sourceJobId: string (links back to contractor's CRM job)
  verifiedByContractor: boolean
```

## Authentication Model
- Homeowner creates ZAFTO HOME account (email/password or SSO)
- Account is independent of any contractor
- Contractor "links" to homeowner's property when they do work (similar to how current Client Portal invitation works)
- Multiple contractors can be linked to one property
- Homeowner can revoke contractor access anytime

# GO-TO-MARKET STRATEGY

## Phase 1: Stealth Launch (Now â†’ 6 months)
**Don't announce the platform pivot. Just ship features.**

- Rebrand Client Portal â†’ "Home Portal" in the UI
- Add "Your Property" as the anchor feature (already built)
- Equipment Passport with auto-population from CRM jobs
- Document vault consolidation
- Homeowner can create account directly (not just contractor invitation)
- Position to contractors as: "Your clients get a better experience, which means better retention"

**Key message to contractors**: "We're giving your clients a reason to stay with you."

## Phase 2: Premium Launch (6-12 months)
- Launch AI Property Advisor (Claude API integration â€” you already have this pattern from the CRM)
- Quote comparison tool (initially just for the homeowner's own quotes, not marketplace)
- Smart alerts and maintenance calendar
- $7.99/month pricing, 30-day free trial
- Market directly to homeowners through contractor's client base

**Key message to homeowners**: "Your home finally has a brain."

## Phase 3: Marketplace (12-18 months)
- Open service request marketplace
- Preferred contractor first-look system
- Lead generation for contractors
- Featured placement ads
- Begin direct homeowner acquisition (not just through contractors)

**Key message to contractors**: "More clients finding you, not you finding clients."
**Key message to homeowners**: "The best contractors compete for your business."

## Phase 4: Platform (18-24 months)
- Property sale transfer feature (real estate play)
- Insurance integration (property record â†’ better rates)
- Home equity / renovation financing partnerships
- Multi-property management
- API for third-party integrations

# COMPETITIVE LANDSCAPE

| Company | What They Do | Why ZAFTO Wins |
|---------|-------------|----------------|
| **HomeAdvisor/Angi** | Lead gen marketplace | No property record, no data continuity, contractors hate the lead quality |
| **Thumbtack** | Service marketplace | Same as above â€” transactional, no relationship |
| **Notion/Google Docs** | DIY home records | Manual, no auto-population, no AI, no contractor integration |
| **Hippo/Kin** | Insurance + home monitoring | Focused on insurance, not service management |
| **Frontdoor (AHS)** | Home warranties | Narrow scope, terrible contractor networks |
| **Apple Home** | Smart home control | Devices only, no service/maintenance layer |

**Nobody has built the Carfax for homes.** Nobody has the data pipeline that ZAFTO already has through its CRM. The closest attempt is scattered across insurance companies, warranty providers, and marketplace platforms â€” none of which talk to each other.

---

# THE MOAT

1. **Data flywheel**: Every contractor job auto-populates homeowner records â†’ more valuable records â†’ more homeowners â†’ more contractors â†’ more data
2. **Switching cost**: 10 years of property history is nearly impossible to recreate. The homeowner will never leave.
3. **Two-sided network**: Homeowners attract contractors. Contractors attract homeowners. Both attract more of both.
4. **AI advantage**: The AI gets smarter with more property data across the entire network. "Water heaters of this model fail at year 9 in your climate zone" â€” only possible with aggregate data.
5. **Contractor relationship**: Unlike pure marketplaces, ZAFTO already has deep trust with contractors through the CRM. This isn't an adversarial marketplace â€” it's an extension of an existing relationship.

---

# RISK REGISTER

| Risk | Severity | Mitigation |
|------|----------|------------|
| Contractor revolt â€” "you're helping clients leave us" | **CRITICAL** | Preferred Contractor advantage, 24hr first-look, intelligence feed. Frame as retention tool, not shopping tool. |
| Slow homeowner adoption | Medium | Auto-creation through contractor CRM. Homeowner gets value without doing anything. |
| Competitor copies the model | Medium | Data flywheel is the moat. First mover with contractor relationships wins. |
| AI gives bad advice ("don't repair, replace") that angers contractors | High | AI always recommends consulting preferred contractor. Never says "switch contractors." |
| Privacy/data concerns | Medium | Transparent data policy. Full export. Full delete. GDPR-compliant from day one. |
| Homeowners game the quote system | Low | Verified quotes only. Rate limiting. Contractor feedback on lead quality. |

---

# NAMING

**Home Portal** â€” simple, clear, positions alongside ZAFTO Trades (contractor CRM), ZAFTO Legal, ZAFTO Business.

Domain: `home.zafto.app` or `my.zafto.app`
App: Home Portal (iOS/Android/Web)
Tagline candidates:
- "Your home's permanent record"
- "Every home deserves a brain"
- "Own your home's story"

1. **Finalize the contractor messaging** â€” this needs to be bulletproof before any public-facing changes
2. **Rename Client Portal â†’ Home Portal** in the codebase
3. **Add direct homeowner registration** (not just contractor invitation)
4. **Build Equipment Passport auto-population** from CRM job completions
5. **Design the Preferred Contractor system** â€” this is what makes contractors feel safe
6. **Prototype AI Property Advisor** â€” single chat interface, property-aware context

# APPENDIX A: CONTRACTOR TRUST ARCHITECTURE

## The Core Problem

You can build the most contractor-friendly system on earth, but if the contractor's gut reaction when they hear "your clients can shop around" is fear â€” you've already lost. The protection has to be **visible, felt, and controllable** â€” not buried in a terms of service page.

---

## Principle 1: SHOW THEM THE SHIELD IN REAL TIME

The contractor dashboard needs a dedicated section â€” call it "Client Loyalty" or "Your Advantage" â€” that makes the protection tangible with live numbers.

### What the contractor sees in their CRM dashboard:

```
â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”

That screen is worth more than any sales pitch. The contractor doesn't have to trust your words â€” they can see the data. Every month they see "0 clients left" and "12 requests came to me first," the fear dissolves.

The contractor sees: I got first dibs. I have 24 hours. I know this client's full history. No other contractor has this context. The advantage is obvious.

---

## Principle 2: GIVE THEM THE KILL SWITCH

Fear comes from lack of control. Eliminate the fear by giving contractors a choice they'll almost never use.

### Marketplace Participation Toggle

```
Client Marketplace Settings
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

When your clients request quotes:

  â—‰ Preferred + Marketplace (recommended)
    You get 24hr first-look on all requests.
    If you decline, client can see other options.

  â—‹ Preferred Only
    Your clients only see you. No marketplace.
    They can still manually find other contractors
    outside ZAFTO, but we won't help them.

  â—‹ Open
    No preferred advantage. Clients see all
    contractors equally. (Not recommended.)
```

**Why this works:** Most contractors will pick "Preferred + Marketplace" because they realize the first-look advantage is powerful. But having the "Preferred Only" option means they never feel trapped. They're choosing to participate, not being forced.

**The psychology:** Knowing you CAN lock it down makes you less likely to actually lock it down. It's like a gym membership cancellation policy â€” easy cancellation increases retention because it removes the anxiety.

**The business reality:** Even "Preferred Only" contractors still benefit from Home Portal because their clients have better records, better engagement, and better retention. And those contractors' clients who DO want to shop around will just use Google anyway â€” at least with marketplace enabled, the contractor gets first-look.

---

## Principle 3: MAKE THEM MONEY THEY WEREN'T MAKING BEFORE

The single most powerful way to eliminate fear is to make the contractor more profitable than they were before Home Portal existed.

**The contractor's internal math becomes:** "Home Portal generates me $4,200/month in work I would have missed. Why would I fight this?"

This is the argument that ends the conversation. Not "trust us" â€” but "look at your bank account."

### Marketplace Inbound Leads (New Revenue)

Contractors also receive leads from homeowners who DON'T have a preferred contractor â€” people who signed up for Home Portal directly, moved to a new area, or whose previous contractor retired.

```
â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”

```

**The message:** Marketplace isn't about losing clients â€” it's about gaining new ones. The contractor now sees Home Portal as a lead source, not a threat.

---

## Principle 4: TRANSPARENT RULES, NOT BLACK BOX

Contractors hate algorithms they don't understand. Publish the rules. Make them simple. Let the contractor verify them.

### The Home Portal Contractor Promise (Published Publicly)

```
HOW ZAFTO HOME PROTECTS YOUR BUSINESS

1. YOU ALWAYS COME FIRST
   When your client needs service, you are the first
   and only contractor they see for 24 hours.

2. YOUR HISTORY IS YOUR WEAPON
   Your service record with each client is visible
   to them. No competitor can fabricate that trust.

3. YOU CONTROL YOUR PARTICIPATION
   You choose whether your clients can access the
   marketplace. You can change this anytime.

4. WE NEVER UNDERCUT YOU
   The AI will never tell a homeowner your price is
   too high. It provides market context, not judgment.

5. WE NEVER RECOMMEND SWITCHING
   The AI will never suggest a homeowner try a
   different contractor. Switching is always the
   homeowner's initiative, never ours.

6. YOU SEE WHAT THEY SEE
   If a client requests marketplace quotes, you're
   notified immediately. No surprises.

7. YOUR DATA IS YOURS
   Your pricing, margins, and internal notes are
   never visible to homeowners or competitors.
```

Print this. Put it on the website. Put it in the contractor onboarding. Put it in the CRM dashboard. Make it impossible to miss.

---

## Principle 5: LET CONTRACTORS SHAPE THE RULES

### Contractor Advisory Board

Before launching Home Portal publicly, recruit 10-15 existing CRM contractors into an advisory board:

- Show them the product vision
- Let them red-team every feature ("how could this hurt me?")
- Give them input on the rules (24hr first-look vs 48hr? What data is shared?)
- Give them early access to shape their experience
- Name them as founding advisors (ego, ownership, investment)

**Why this works:** A contractor who helped BUILD the rules will never feel threatened by them. They'll defend the platform to other contractors because it's partly theirs.

### Beta Rollout Through Existing Contractors

Don't launch Home Portal to random homeowners. Launch it through your best contractors:

1. Contractor invites their own clients to Home Portal
2. Clients see contractor as their preferred provider from day one
3. Contractor sees the loyalty dashboard light up with their clients
4. Contractor experiences the revenue opportunity alerts
5. THEN â€” months later â€” open the marketplace for unattached homeowners

The contractor's first experience with Home Portal is their clients being MORE connected to them, not less. By the time the marketplace exists, the contractor has months of proof that the system works in their favor.

---

## Principle 6: THE AI NEVER BETRAYS THE CONTRACTOR

This is subtle but critical. The AI Property Advisor must be carefully prompted to protect the contractor relationship.

### What the AI DOES say:

- "Your water heater is approaching end-of-life. Average lifespan for this model is 10-12 years. Here's what to consider when deciding to repair vs replace."
- "This quote is within the typical range for this type of work in your area."
- "I'd recommend discussing this with your electrician at [Preferred Contractor Name] â€” they know your system best."
- "Based on your property, you may qualify for these rebates: [list]"
- "Here are the questions to ask your contractor about this repair."

### What the AI NEVER says:
- ~~"This quote seems high. You should get other quotes."~~
- ~~"Other contractors in your area charge less for this."~~
- ~~"You might want to consider switching to a different provider."~~
- ~~"Your contractor missed this issue."~~
- ~~"I can find you a better contractor."~~

### The AI's Role in the Contractor Relationship:

The AI is the homeowner's **property advisor**, not their **contractor shopping assistant**. It helps them understand their home, make informed decisions, and have better conversations with their contractor. It makes the homeowner a BETTER client â€” more informed, more realistic about costs, more proactive about maintenance.

**The contractor benefits from an educated client.** Educated clients:
- Approve work faster (they understand why it's needed)
- Have realistic budget expectations (AI showed them market ranges)
- Do proactive maintenance (more recurring revenue)
- Don't blame the contractor when equipment fails at end-of-life
- Refer more confidently ("my ZAFTO record shows exactly what they did")

---

## The Rollout Conversation With Contractors

When you tell contractors about Home Portal, lead with what they GET, not what homeowners get.

### DON'T say:
"We're building a platform where homeowners own their property records and can shop for contractors."

### DO say:
"We're adding features to your CRM that help you keep clients longer and find new revenue you're currently missing."

Then show them:
1. Revenue opportunity alerts ("your client's water heater is dying â€” here's a $3K job waiting for you")
2. Loyalty dashboard ("47 clients, 100% retention, you're their preferred contractor")
3. First-look advantage ("you see every request 24 hours before anyone else")
4. Inbound marketplace leads ("new homeowners in your area with no contractor â€” want them?")

The homeowner side of the story comes AFTER they've absorbed the value. By then, their reaction is "oh, and the homeowner gets a nice app too? Cool, that makes them stickier."

---

## Worst-Case Scenarios & Responses

### Scenario: Contractor says "I don't want my clients on this at all"
**Response:** "That's completely your choice. You can turn off marketplace for your clients with one toggle. They'll still get the property record (which keeps them engaged with YOU), but they'll never see other contractors through ZAFTO. You can change this anytime."

### Scenario: A client uses Home Portal to leave a contractor
**Response:** "That client was going to leave anyway â€” they would have used Google, Yelp, or their neighbor's recommendation. At least with ZAFTO, you got a 24-hour warning and the chance to save the relationship. Without ZAFTO, you'd have just lost them silently."

### Scenario: A contractor sees their client request marketplace quotes
**Response:** "You have 24 hours to respond first. You know this client's full history, you have the relationship, and your 5-star record with them is visible. If you give a fair quote, you win. If you don't, that's important market feedback."

### Scenario: Competitor contractor undercuts significantly on a quote
**Response:** "The AI tells the homeowner context, not just price. 'Contractor A quotes $8,400 with a 5-year warranty and has completed 6 jobs for you with a 5.0 rating. Contractor B quotes $6,200 with a 1-year warranty and is new to the platform.' Your track record is worth more than a discount."

---

*End of Appendix A â€” Contractor Trust Architecture*


---

## APPENDIX B â€” PROJECT INTELLIGENCE & AI PRICING SYSTEM

### The Vision

Every homeowner should be able to explore any home improvement project â€” patio, landscaping, roofing, plumbing, basement finish, bathroom addition, literally everything â€” and get accurate, regionally-specific cost intelligence BEFORE talking to a contractor.

This is NOT a quoting tool. This is **education**. The framing matters:
- NOT: "Here's your quote" (replaces contractor = contractor revolt)
- YES: "Here's what this project typically costs in your area so you're informed before talking to anyone"

Informed homeowners are BETTER clients â€” they waste less contractor time, have realistic budgets, and make faster decisions. Contractors prefer educated buyers.

### How Pricing Accuracy Works

The AI isn't guessing. It synthesizes actual data sources:

| Data Source | What It Provides | Update Frequency |
|-------------|-----------------|-----------------|
| BLS Regional Labor Rates | Hourly labor costs by trade, by metro area | Quarterly |
| RSMeans Cost Database | Industry-standard material + labor costs | Annual |
| Remodeling Magazine Cost vs. Value | Project costs by metro area, ROI data | Annual |
| State Permit Records | Actual project costs (often public record) | Ongoing |
| ZAFTO CRM Aggregate Data | Real job costs from our own contractors (anonymized) | Real-time |
| Material Supplier APIs | Current material pricing | Weekly |
| Census/Property Data | Home age, sq footage, regional factors | Static + updates |

### User Experience Flow

```
1. Homeowner says: "I want to finish my basement"

2. AI knows the property context:
   - 1,800 sq ft ranch, built 1992, Hartford CT
   - Existing electrical: 200A panel (from equipment passport)
   - No existing plumbing in basement (from property profile)

3. AI returns Project Intelligence:
   â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”
   â”‚  BASEMENT FINISHING â€” Hartford, CT              â”‚
   â”‚                                                  â”‚
   â”‚  Typical Range: $28,000 â€“ $52,000               â”‚
   â”‚  Your Area Average: $38,500                      â”‚
   â”‚  (based on 127 similar projects in Hartford metro)â”‚
   â”‚                                                  â”‚
   â”‚  WHAT'S INCLUDED AT EACH TIER:                  â”‚
   â”‚                                                  â”‚
   â”‚  Basic ($28-34K):                               â”‚
   â”‚  â€¢ Framing, drywall, flooring                   â”‚
   â”‚  â€¢ 3-4 recessed lights, basic outlets           â”‚
   â”‚  â€¢ No bathroom, no wet bar                      â”‚
   â”‚                                                  â”‚
   â”‚  Mid-Range ($35-44K):                           â”‚
   â”‚  â€¢ Everything above + half bath                 â”‚
   â”‚  â€¢ Better flooring (LVP vs carpet)              â”‚
   â”‚  â€¢ Egress window, more lighting                 â”‚
   â”‚                                                  â”‚
   â”‚  Premium ($45-52K+):                            â”‚
   â”‚  â€¢ Everything above + full bath                 â”‚
   â”‚  â€¢ Wet bar, built-in entertainment              â”‚
   â”‚  â€¢ Heated flooring, dedicated HVAC zone         â”‚
   â”‚                                                  â”‚
   â”‚  WHAT DRIVES COST UP/DOWN:                      â”‚
   â”‚  â–² Adding bathroom (+$8-15K plumbing/permits)   â”‚
   â”‚  â–² Low ceiling height (more complex framing)    â”‚
   â”‚  â–¼ Open floor plan (less framing/drywall)       â”‚

   â”‚                                                  â”‚
   â”‚  TIMELINE: 6-10 weeks typical                   â”‚
   â”‚  PERMITS: Yes â€” building + electrical required   â”‚
   â”‚  ROI: Recoups ~70% at resale (Hartford avg)     â”‚
   â”‚                                                  â”‚
   â”‚  [Get Real Quotes]  [Save to My Projects]       â”‚
   â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜

4. "Get Real Quotes" â†’ feeds into marketplace
   - Preferred contractor gets 24hr first-look
   - Or opens to directory if no preferred contractor
```

### The Funnel

This is the top of the Home Portal marketplace funnel:

```
Homeowner explores project idea
         â”‚
         â–¼
Project Intelligence (AI cost range, scope, timeline, ROI)
         â”‚
         â–¼
Homeowner is educated and ready
         â”‚
         â–¼
"Get Real Quotes" button
         â”‚
         â”œâ”€â”€â–º Has preferred contractor â†’ 24hr first-look
         â”‚
         â””â”€â”€â–º No preferred contractor â†’ marketplace directory
                    â”‚
                    â–¼
              Contractor pays for lead
```

Nobody opens an app to "manage their property record." But they absolutely open it to find out "how much does it cost to add a second bathroom?" Project Intelligence is the hook.

### National Contractor Directory

**The Problem:** ZAFTO has zero marketplace contractors right now. CRM customers are the seed but not enough for national coverage.

**The Solution:** Aggregate a national directory from public data sources, then tier by trust level.

**Public Data Sources for Directory Population:**

| Source | Data Available | Coverage |
|--------|---------------|----------|
| State Licensing Boards | Name, license #, trade, status, violations | Every state (public record) |
| BBB Listings | Business name, rating, complaints | National |
| Google Business Profiles | Name, reviews, location, photos | National |
| Building Permit Records | Contractor name on permits (often public) | County-level |
| Trade Association Directories | NECA (electrical), PHCC (plumbing), ACCA (HVAC), NRCA (roofing) | National |
| Secretary of State Filings | Business registration, LLC/Corp status | Every state |

### Contractor Trust Tiers

| Tier | Badge | What It Means | How They Get There |
|------|-------|--------------|-------------------|
| **ZAFTO Verified** | Gold shield | Uses ZAFTO CRM, real job history, real reviews, equipment records | Existing CRM customers |
| **Claimed Profile** | Blue check | Contractor claimed listing, added portfolio, verified license | Self-service signup + verification |
| **Listed** | Gray | Public record only â€” name, license, trade, location | Auto-populated from licensing data |

**The Strategic Advantage:** ZAFTO Verified contractors look dramatically better than Listed contractors. Real job history, real equipment install records, actual client reviews through the platform, response time metrics. This makes CRM adoption MORE attractive, not less â€” being on ZAFTO CRM is now a competitive advantage in the marketplace.

### AI Database Architecture (Three Systems)

Each platform surface needs its own AI context and knowledge base:

| System | AI Role | Knowledge Needed |
|--------|---------|-----------------|
| **ZAFTO Trades (CRM)** | Business assistant for contractors | Company data, pricing, bids, jobs, codes, calculators |
| **Home Portal (Client Portal)** | Property advisor for homeowners | Property data, equipment, regional costs, project intelligence |
| **ZAFTO Mobile App** | Field assistant for crews | Job details, codes, calculators, voice entry, equipment scanning |

Each AI instance draws from shared data (Firestore) but has different context, permissions, personality, and guardrails. The contractor AI sees margins and costs. The homeowner AI sees project ranges and recommendations. The field AI sees job-specific details and code references.

**This architecture will be designed and built after Firestore wiring is complete.** The data layer must exist before the AI layer can consume it.

### AI Pricing Guardrails

**AI DOES say:**
- "Basement finishing in Hartford typically costs $28,000â€“$52,000"
- "Adding a bathroom increases cost by $8,000â€“$15,000"
- "This project typically recoups about 70% at resale"
- "Here are questions to ask contractors when getting quotes"
- "Based on 127 similar projects in your metro area"

**AI NEVER says:**
- ~~"This contractor is charging too much"~~
- ~~"You should pay no more than $X"~~
- ~~"This quote is overpriced"~~
- ~~"I can give you an exact quote"~~
- ~~"You don't need a contractor for this"~~

The AI helps homeowners understand what things cost. It never judges a specific contractor's pricing or recommends DIY over professional work.

### CLOUD FUNCTIONS â€” The Only Live AI

**Status: DEPLOYED AND WORKING**

5 AI endpoints live on Firebase (`zafto-2b563`), using Anthropic SDK with `claude-sonnet-4-20250514`:

| Endpoint | What It Does | Status |
|----------|-------------|--------|
| `analyzePanel` | Electrical panel photo â†’ structured analysis | LIVE |
| `analyzeNameplate` | Equipment nameplate â†’ make/model/serial extraction | LIVE |
| `analyzeWire` | Wire/conductor photo â†’ identification | LIVE |
| `analyzeViolation` | Photo â†’ NEC code violation detection | LIVE |
| `smartScan` | Auto-detect photo type â†’ route to correct analyzer | LIVE |

Has: credit system, caching, error handling, safety guardrails, confidence thresholds.
Model: `claude-sonnet-4-20250514`, max 2048 tokens, min 0.4 confidence.

---

### MOBILE APP â€” Built But Dormant

**Status: SUBSTANTIAL CODE EXISTS, NEEDS FIRESTORE WIRING TO FUNCTION**

| File | Lines | What It Does | Status |
|------|:-----:|-------------|--------|
| `services/ai_service.dart` | 260 | Image analysis service, talks to Cloud Functions | WORKS (uses deployed functions) |
| `services/ai/ai_conversation_service.dart` | 549 | Full Riverpod conversation handler, Firestore persistence, streaming, photo context, tool execution | BUILT, needs Firestore |
| `services/ai/ai_tools.dart` | 558 | Tool registry: calculator search, NEC reference, job CRUD, customer lookup, invoice drafts, business metrics | BUILT, needs real data |
| `services/ai/system_prompt_builder.dart` | 459 | Context-aware prompt builder (user, company, job, customer, role, permissions) | BUILT |
| `models/ai_conversation.dart` | 503 | Conversation + Message models, attachments, tool calls | BUILT |
| `screens/ai/ai_chat_screen.dart` | 1,005 | Full chat UI with photo attachments, typing indicators, suggested follow-ups | BUILT |
| `widgets/zafto/zafto_ai_bar.dart` | 450 | AI-first input bar (replaces search) | BUILT |

**Total: ~3,784 lines of AI code in the mobile app.**

The conversation service calls Cloud Functions, which call Anthropic API. The architecture is correct â€” mobile never calls Claude directly. But because Firestore isn't wired, the conversation service can't persist threads, load company context, or execute tool calls against real data.

The image scanning (ai_service.dart) DOES work because it talks directly to the deployed Cloud Functions.

### SPEC vs REALITY

| Spec (doc 23) | Reality |
|---------------|---------|
| "ZaftoAIService â€” single entry point for ALL AI" | Mobile has this architecture. Web has nothing. |
| Thread model with Firestore persistence | Model exists in mobile. Zero implementation in web. |
| Audit log for every AI action | Defined in spec. Not implemented anywhere. |
| Tool registry (calculators, NEC, jobs, customers) | Built in mobile (558 lines). Not in web. |
| Context-aware system prompts | Built in mobile (459 lines). Not in web. |
| Three action tiers (Green/Yellow/Red) | Defined in spec. Not enforced anywhere. |
| Usage tracking and rate limits | Credit system exists in Cloud Functions for scans. No conversation limits. |
| Conversation summaries at >20 messages | Defined in spec. Not implemented. |

**The spec (2,772 lines) is thorough and well-designed. The mobile app has ~70% of the architecture built. The web apps have 0%.**

---

### WHAT NEEDS TO HAPPEN (Post-Firestore Wiring)

Each system needs its own AI layer. They share the same Firestore data but have different:
- Context (contractor vs homeowner vs field crew)
- Permissions (contractor sees margins, homeowner doesn't)
- Tools (contractor creates bids, homeowner requests quotes)
- Personality (business assistant vs property advisor vs field helper)
- Guardrails (what each AI can and cannot say)

| System | AI To Build | Depends On |
|--------|------------|------------|
| **Web Portal CRM** | Replace mock responses with real Cloud Function calls. Port tool registry from mobile. Add web-specific tools (reports, team management). | Firestore wiring |
| **Client Portal / Home Portal** | Build AI Property Advisor from scratch. Project Intelligence engine. Regional cost database integration. Marketplace recommendation logic. | Firestore wiring + Home Portal features |
| **Mobile App** | Wire existing conversation service to Firestore. Test tool execution with real data. Voice input (future). | Firestore wiring |
| **Cloud Functions** | Add conversation endpoint (not just image analysis). Shared AI backend for all three frontends. | Current functions work, extend them |

**Priority order after wiring:**
1. Mobile AI activation (most code exists, smallest gap)
2. Web Portal CRM AI (port from mobile, add web tools)
3. Client Portal / Home Portal AI (build from scratch, biggest project)

## APPENDIX D â€” ADVANCED HOME INTELLIGENCE FEATURES
### Added: February 4, 2026

### Overview

These features transform Home Portal from a service record into a **living home management platform** â€” the kind of thing homeowners check monthly because it provides unique value they can't get anywhere else. The moat only exists if the homeowner feels this belongs to THEM.


---

### Feature 1: AI History Onboarding

**The problem:** When a homeowner joins Home Portal, their property record is empty. If they don't already have a ZAFTO contractor feeding data in, there's no service history, no equipment records, nothing. That's a cold start problem that kills adoption.

**The solution:** AI-powered property research that builds a baseline profile from public data sources before the homeowner lifts a finger.

**What the AI can pull from public records:**

| Data Source | What It Contains | Availability |
|-------------|-----------------|--------------|
| County Assessor/Tax Records | Year built, sq footage, lot size, construction type, bedrooms/bathrooms, assessed value history | Nearly universal â€” every county has this |
| Building Permit Records | Major renovations, additions, electrical upgrades, HVAC installs, roofing, plumbing â€” with dates and contractor names | Most counties, many digitized |
| Property Deed/Transfer Records | Ownership history, sale prices, transfer dates | Public record everywhere |
| MLS/Zillow/Redfin Listing History | Past listing photos, descriptions, features mentioned, price history | Widely available |
| FEMA Flood Maps | Flood zone status, flood risk | National coverage |
| EPA Environmental Records | Environmental hazards, nearby contamination | National database |
| Local Code Requirements | What code version the home was built under, what's been updated since | By jurisdiction |
| Utility Provider Data | Average energy usage (with homeowner permission via Green Button) | Growing availability |
| HOA Records | Restrictions, assessments, common area maintenance | Where applicable |

**Onboarding Flow:**

```
Step 1: Homeowner enters address
        â†“
Step 2: AI searches public records (5-15 seconds)
        â†“
Step 3: AI presents findings:

â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”
â”‚  WE FOUND YOUR HOME                                 â”‚
â”‚                                                     â”‚
â”‚  42 Oak Street, Hartford CT 06106                   â”‚
â”‚  Built: 1994 | 2,400 sq ft | Colonial              â”‚
â”‚  4 bed / 2.5 bath | 0.31 acre lot                   â”‚
â”‚                                                     â”‚
â”‚  CONSTRUCTION HISTORY WE FOUND:                     â”‚
â”‚                                                     â”‚
â”‚  1994 â€” Original construction                       â”‚
â”‚         Builder: Hartford Development Corp          â”‚

â”‚                                                     â”‚

â”‚         Contractor: New England Roofing             â”‚

â”‚                                                     â”‚

â”‚         Contractor: ComfortAir Solutions            â”‚
â”‚         Permit #18-2201                             â”‚
â”‚                                                     â”‚
â”‚  2021 â€” Bathroom renovation (2nd floor)             â”‚
â”‚         Permit #21-0447                             â”‚
â”‚                                                     â”‚
â”‚  ESTIMATED CURRENT SYSTEMS:                         â”‚
â”‚  Electrical: 200A panel (~21 years old)             â”‚
â”‚  HVAC: ~6 years old (typical lifespan: 15-20)      â”‚
â”‚  Roof: ~13 years old (typical lifespan: 20-25)     â”‚
â”‚  Water Heater: Unknown â€” add manually or scan       â”‚
â”‚                                                     â”‚
â”‚  [Looks Right â€” Save]    [Edit Details]             â”‚
â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜

Step 4: Homeowner confirms/corrects
        â†“
Step 5: AI generates initial health estimates + maintenance timeline
```

**What makes this powerful:**
- Homeowner gets a populated profile in under 60 seconds
- Historical permit data reveals what systems were upgraded and when
- AI can estimate equipment age from permit dates ("HVAC replaced 2018 = ~6 years old")
- Gaps become obvious: "No plumbing permits found since construction â€” original pipes likely 30 years old"
- The contractor listed on those permits? Natural connection point for marketplace

**How deep can it go?**
- Original construction: Almost always available (assessor records go back to the building)
- Major renovations: Anything that required a permit â€” additions, system replacements, structural work
- Ownership timeline: Every sale, every transfer, every price point
- Assessed value jumps: A sudden $40K increase in 2015 suggests a major renovation that year
- Listing descriptions: MLS data often says "new kitchen 2019" or "updated HVAC" â€” AI can parse this
- Some counties have permit records going back 50+ years in digital archives

**What it WON'T catch:**
- Unpermitted work (but the gaps themselves are informative â€” "no electrical permit since 1994 but panel looks newer? Might be unpermitted")
- Cosmetic work (paint, flooring, fixtures â€” no permits required)
- Equipment details (make/model/serial â€” only install dates)
- Quality of work (permits prove it was done, not how well)

**Data accuracy approach:**
- Present everything as "we found this in public records" â€” not "this is fact"
- Let homeowner confirm, correct, or add missing info
- Flag confidence levels: HIGH (assessor data), MEDIUM (permit records), LOW (estimated from age/value changes)
- Over time, ZAFTO contractor jobs replace estimates with verified data

**Technical implementation:**
- API aggregation layer that queries county assessor APIs, permit portals, and property data providers
- Start with major metros (top 50 MSAs cover ~55% of US population)
- Use ATTOM Data, CoreLogic, or similar property data APIs for baseline
- Supplement with direct county portal scraping where APIs don't exist
- Cache results â€” property history doesn't change often

---

**How it calculates:**
- Equipment ages + manufacturer-recommended maintenance schedules
- Regional cost averages (from Project Intelligence data in Appendix B)
- Historical spend from service records
- Industry data on replacement timelines by climate zone
- AI adjusts as real service data flows in

**Revenue angle:** Premium feature ($7.99/mo tier). Homeowners who budget for maintenance are better contractor clients â€” they approve work faster, don't argue about costs, and schedule proactively instead of calling in emergencies.

---

### Feature 3: Home Performance Index

**What it is:** A numerical score (0-100) that represents the overall health, maintenance status, and risk profile of a home. Think credit score, but for your property.

**How it's calculated:**

| Factor | Weight | Example |
|--------|:------:|---------|
| Equipment age vs lifespan | 25% | All systems under 50% lifespan = high score |
| Maintenance compliance | 20% | Regular inspections done on time = high score |
| Service history completeness | 15% | Full records vs gaps = higher confidence |
| Code compliance | 15% | Up to current code vs original 1994 code |
| Risk factors | 15% | Flood zone, recalled equipment, deferred maintenance |
| Energy efficiency | 10% | Modern systems, insulation, windows |

**Score ranges:**

| Score | Label | What It Means |
|:-----:|-------|---------------|
| 90-100 | Excellent | Well-maintained, modern systems, low risk |
| 75-89 | Good | Minor maintenance needed, systems healthy |
| 60-74 | Fair | Some deferred maintenance, aging systems |
| 40-59 | Needs Attention | Multiple systems approaching end-of-life |
| 0-39 | Critical | Significant deferred maintenance, high risk |

**Why this matters beyond ZAFTO:**
- **Insurance integration (future):** Insurers want to know property condition. A verified Home Performance Index from ZAFTO (backed by real service records, not self-reporting) could influence premiums. Homeowners with 85+ scores could qualify for discounts. Partnership play with insurers.
- **Real estate transactions:** Sellers can show their score. Buyers can request it. "This home has a ZAFTO Performance Index of 91" carries weight.
- **Home equity/lending:** Banks assessing property condition for HELOCs or refinancing could use this as a data point.

**Privacy control:** Homeowner chooses whether their score is private, shareable via link, or public. Always opt-in, never exposed without consent.

---

### Feature 4: Certified Service Passport

**What it is:** A verified, exportable record that proves the quality and compliance of all work done on a property.

**What's in it:**

| Record | Source | Verification Level |
|--------|--------|-------------------|
| Work performed (scope, materials, labor) | ZAFTO CRM job completion | ZAFTO Verified |
| Contractor license status at time of work | State licensing board cross-reference | Auto-verified |
| Permit records | County permit data (Feature 1 onboarding) | Public record |
| Inspection results | Linked inspection reports from ZAFTO CRM | ZAFTO Verified |
| Equipment installed (make, model, serial) | Equipment Passport entries | Contractor-entered |
| Warranty documentation | Uploaded documents, manufacturer data | Document-backed |
| Compliance certificates | Contractor uploads, linked to job | Document-backed |
| Safety alerts addressed | Recall responses, code updates applied | Tracked in system |

**Export formats:**
- PDF report (printable, shareable, professional)
- Structured data (JSON/CSV for insurance, real estate, or API consumers)
- Shareable link (view-only, time-limited or permanent)

**Use cases:**
- Selling a home: "Here's every licensed professional who worked on this property, every permit pulled, every inspection passed"
- Insurance claims: "Here's the documented service history proving regular maintenance"
- Contractor reputation: Jobs on Certified Passports count toward their ZAFTO rating

---

**Data principles:**
- All aggregate data is anonymized â€” no individual homeowner data exposed
- Minimum threshold before showing insights (e.g., need 50+ data points per metro for cost averages)
- Homeowners can opt out of contributing to aggregate data
- Contractors never see individual homeowner data through aggregate views

**Why this is a moat:** This data gets better with every homeowner and contractor on the platform. A competitor starting from zero can't replicate "9,000 Carrier units across 200 climate zones with real failure data." Compounding network effect.

### Feature 6: Risk Alerts

**What it does:** Proactive safety and compliance notifications that go beyond basic maintenance reminders.

**Alert types:**

| Alert | Source | Example |
|-------|--------|---------|
| Equipment recalls | CPSC database, manufacturer bulletins | "Your Carrier furnace model has been recalled for heat exchanger defect" |
| Code updates | Local code adoption tracking | "Hartford adopted 2023 NEC. Your panel was installed under 2014 code â€” not a violation, but newer protections available" |
| Safety risks | Equipment age + failure data | "CO risk increases for furnaces over 15 years. Yours is 14. Schedule CO detector check and furnace inspection" |
| Weather-driven | NOAA data + property profile | "Freeze warning tonight. Your outdoor pipes have no insulation record â€” consider covering exposed faucets" |
| Environmental | EPA + local data | "Your home is in a radon zone 1 area. No radon test on record â€” recommended every 2 years" |
| Insurance-relevant | Claim pattern data | "Homes built 1990-1999 in your area have elevated polybutylene pipe failure rates. Check plumbing material" |

**Notification behavior:**
- Critical safety alerts: Push notification + email + in-app banner
- Compliance updates: In-app notification + monthly digest email
- Seasonal/weather: In-app notification, timing based on forecast
- Homeowner controls frequency and channels in settings

| Risk Alerts | Critical safety only (recalls) | All alert types + customizable notifications |

### The Identity Shift

These features collectively change what Home Portal IS in the homeowner's mind:

| Without These | With These |
|---------------|-----------|
| "An app my contractor gave me" | "Where my home lives digitally" |
| "I check it when I get a bill" | "I check it monthly for insights" |
| Open it 2x/year | Open it 2x/month |
| Replaceable | Irreplaceable (10 years of data) |
| Contractor's tool | MY tool |

The moat only exists if the homeowner feels this belongs to THEM and gives them value they can't get anywhere else.

### Feature 7: Emergency Home Profile

**The problem:** It's 2 AM, a pipe bursts, water is spraying everywhere. Where's the main water shutoff? Where's the gas shutoff? Where's the electrical panel? Most homeowners don't know â€” and they're not going to search for it during a crisis.

**What it is:** A dedicated emergency section with photos and locations of every critical shutoff and access point in the home.

**What's documented:**

| Item | Info Stored | Why It Matters |
|------|------------|----------------|
| Main water shutoff | Photo, location description, valve type (gate/ball) | Burst pipes, flooding |
| Gas shutoff | Photo, location, tool needed (wrench?) | Gas leak, smell of gas |
| Electrical main panel | Photo, location, main breaker labeled | Electrical emergency, fire |
| Individual circuit map | Photo of panel schedule + labeled descriptions | Targeted shutoffs without killing whole house |
| Sump pump | Photo, location, backup battery status | Basement flooding |
| HVAC emergency shutoff | Photo, location per unit | Furnace malfunction, CO alarm |
| Water heater shutoff | Photo, location, gas vs electric procedure | Leak, overheating |
| Septic/sewer cleanout | Photo, location in yard | Sewage backup |
| Fire extinguisher locations | Photo, type (ABC vs K), expiration dates | Fire |
| Outdoor faucet shutoffs | Photo, interior valve location | Freeze prevention |

**UX:**
- Prominent "EMERGENCY" button â€” always visible, one tap from home screen
- Works offline (cached locally â€” no waiting for network when water is spraying)
- Large text, high contrast, photos dominate â€” designed for panic mode
- Step-by-step shutoff instructions per system
- "Call 911" and "Call Your Contractor" buttons at top

**Sharing:**
- Share access with spouse, partner, adult children, babysitter, housesitter, tenants
- Shareable via link (no app needed for the recipient)
- Print-friendly version for posting near the panel/shutoffs

**Population methods:**
- Contractor fills it in during a job (part of job completion checklist in CRM)
- Homeowner adds manually with phone camera
- AI prompts: "You added a water heater but haven't documented its shutoff location yet"

**Why this is sticky:** This is the one feature that makes someone say "thank GOD I had this" at least once. And they tell everyone about it. Word of mouth gold.

---

### Feature 8: Energy & Rebate Dashboard

**The problem:** The Inflation Reduction Act (IRA), state programs, and utility rebates offer thousands of dollars for home efficiency upgrades â€” heat pumps, insulation, windows, electric panels, solar, water heaters. Most homeowners have no idea what they qualify for or how much they'd save.

**What ZAFTO already knows:**
- Equipment types, ages, and efficiency ratings (Equipment Passport)
- Home construction year and type (Property Profile)
- Location and climate zone (address)
- Household income bracket (optional, for means-tested rebates)

**What the AI can calculate:**

- IRS guidance for federal tax credits (updated annually)
- State energy office programs (varies by state)

- ENERGY STAR specifications for qualifying equipment

**Revenue angle:**
- "Get Quotes" button feeds directly into the marketplace funnel (Appendix B)
- Contractors who sell energy-efficient equipment get preferential placement
- Premium feature â€” free tier shows "you have rebates available," premium shows the full breakdown
- Every rebate-driven upgrade is a contractor job flowing through ZAFTO

**Why now:** Federal rebates from the IRA are active through at least 2032. This is a massive window where homeowners are actively looking for this information. First platform to connect "you qualify for $8K in rebates" â†’ "here's a contractor who can do it" wins.

### Feature 9: Tax Basis Tracker

**The problem:** When you sell your home, capital improvements increase your cost basis, which reduces taxable capital gains. Most homeowners lose receipts, don't know what counts as a capital improvement vs. repair, and overpay on taxes because they can't prove their improvements.

**What ZAFTO already has:** Every job record includes scope of work, cost, date, and contractor. The data is already there â€” it just needs classification.

**How it works:**

**Capital Improvement vs. Repair (IRS definitions):**

| Capital Improvement (adds to basis) | Repair (does NOT add to basis) |
|--------------------------------------|-------------------------------|
| New roof | Patching a roof leak |
| HVAC system replacement | HVAC tune-up or filter change |
| Bathroom addition/remodel | Fixing a leaky faucet |
| Electrical panel upgrade | Replacing an outlet |
| New windows | Re-caulking windows |
| Insulation | Weatherstripping |
| Deck/patio construction | Deck board replacement |
| Landscaping (permanent, e.g., retaining wall) | Mowing, mulching, trimming |

**AI auto-classification:** When a job completes in ZAFTO, the AI flags whether it's likely a capital improvement based on scope of work. Homeowner confirms. Running total maintained automatically.

**Dashboard:**

```
â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”
â”‚  TAX BASIS TRACKER                                  â”‚
â”‚                                                     â”‚
â”‚  Purchase Price (2016): $223,000                    â”‚
â”‚                                                     â”‚
â”‚  Documented Capital Improvements:                   â”‚
â”‚  2018 â€” HVAC replacement: $8,400                    â”‚
â”‚  2019 â€” Bathroom remodel: $12,200                   â”‚
â”‚  2021 â€” Roof replacement: $14,800                   â”‚
â”‚  2023 â€” Electrical panel upgrade: $3,600            â”‚
â”‚                                                     â”‚
â”‚  Adjusted Cost Basis: $262,000                      â”‚
â”‚                                                     â”‚
â”‚  If you sold today at estimated value ($385,000):   â”‚
â”‚  Gain: $123,000                                     â”‚
â”‚  Without tracked improvements: $162,000             â”‚
â”‚  Tax basis savings: $39,000 in documented           â”‚
â”‚  improvements = potential tax savings of $5,850*    â”‚
â”‚                                                     â”‚
â”‚  *Based on 15% capital gains rate.                  â”‚
â”‚  Single filer $250K / married $500K exclusion       â”‚
â”‚  may apply. Consult a tax professional.             â”‚
â”‚                                                     â”‚
â”‚  [Export for Tax Preparer (PDF)]                    â”‚
â”‚  [Add Improvement Not in ZAFTO]                     â”‚
â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜
```

**Disclaimers:** ZAFTO is not a tax advisor. Always includes "consult a tax professional." The tool organizes records and provides estimates â€” it doesn't give tax advice.

**Why this matters:** This feature alone could justify the $7.99/mo premium for anyone planning to sell in the next 5-10 years. The average homeowner has $30-80K in undocumented improvements. At 15% capital gains, that's $4,500-$12,000 in unnecessary taxes. ZAFTO saves them money with data it already has.

---

### Feature 10: Seasonal Maintenance Checklists

**What it is:** AI-generated, personalized, interactive maintenance checklists based on the specific property's equipment, age, climate zone, and service history â€” not generic "winterize your home" articles.

**Example (Fall checklist for a specific home):**

```
â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”
â”‚  FALL CHECKLIST â€” 42 Oak Street                     â”‚
â”‚  Generated for YOUR home | October 2026             â”‚
â”‚                                                     â”‚
â”‚  â˜ Change HVAC filter                               â”‚

**Personalization factors:**
- Equipment specifics (exact filter sizes, model-specific maintenance)
- Service history (what's overdue vs. recently done)
- Climate zone (freeze dates, hurricane season, heat waves)
- Property features (trees = gutter priority, pool = winterization, crawlspace = moisture check)
- Home age (older homes get more structural checks)

**Checklist cadence:** Spring, Summer, Fall, Winter â€” four per year, pushed as notifications at the start of each season. Completion tracked, gamified ("Your home is 83% seasonal-ready").

**Contractor integration:** Any checklist item can be sent directly to the preferred contractor as a service request. Bulk requests: "Send all overdue items to my contractor."

---

### Feature 11: Multi-User Household Access

**The problem:** Homes have more than one person. Both partners need access. Adult children managing elderly parents' homes need access. Tenants need limited access. Property managers need access to multiple units. The current spec has multi-property but not multi-user.

**Permission levels:**

| Role | Can View | Can Edit | Can Request Service | Can Manage Billing | Can Transfer/Delete |
|------|:--------:|:--------:|:-------------------:|:-----------------:|:-------------------:|
| Owner | âœ… | âœ… | âœ… | âœ… | âœ… |
| Co-Owner | âœ… | âœ… | âœ… | âœ… | âŒ |
| Household Member | âœ… | Limited | âœ… | âŒ | âŒ |
| Tenant | Limited | âŒ | Request only | âŒ | âŒ |
| Property Manager | âœ… | âœ… | âœ… | View only | âŒ |
| Guest/Housesitter | Emergency only | âŒ | âŒ | âŒ | âŒ |

**Implementation:**
- Invite by email or link
- Each user has their own ZAFTO account (one account, multiple properties, multiple roles)
- Property-level permissions (you might be Owner on your house and Property Manager on your parents')
- Activity log shows who did what ("Sarah requested HVAC service on Nov 12")
- Owner can revoke access instantly

**Why this matters:** Without multi-user, one person in the household does everything and the other ignores the platform. With multi-user, both people engage. That doubles touchpoints and makes it harder to abandon.

---

### Feature 12: Transfer-with-Property (Full Spec)

**The concept:** When a home sells, the property record transfers to the new owner â€” like a title transfer, but for the home's digital identity. This was mentioned in line 173 as a bullet point. This is the full specification.

**What transfers:**

| Data | Transfers? | Notes |
|------|:----------:|-------|
| Property profile (address, sq ft, year built) | âœ… | Core identity |
| Equipment Passport (all equipment records) | âœ… | New owner needs this |
| Service history (all completed work) | âœ… | But contractor business details redacted |
| Building permit history | âœ… | Public record anyway |
| Home Performance Index history | âœ… | Score trend over time |
| Maintenance budget projections | âœ… | Recalculated for new owner |
| Tax Basis Tracker | âŒ | Stays with seller (their tax records) â€” new owner starts fresh at purchase price |
| Emergency Home Profile | âœ… | Shutoffs don't move when people do |
| Document Vault | Selective | Seller chooses what to include (permits yes, personal invoices optional) |
| Preferred contractor relationships | âŒ | New owner sets their own |
| Personal settings, notifications | âŒ | New owner configures |

**Transfer flow:**

```
SELLER initiates transfer
    â†“
Enters buyer's email
    â†“
Buyer receives invitation:
"The previous owner of 42 Oak Street has transferred
 their Home Portal property record to you.
 This includes 30 years of documented history."
    â†“
Buyer creates account (or links to existing)
    â†“
Buyer reviews transferred data:
"Here's what was transferred. Review and confirm."
    â†“
Transfer complete. Seller's access revoked.
Seller keeps: personal export, tax records
Buyer gets: full property intelligence from day one
```

**Real estate integration (future):**
- Agents can request a "ZAFTO Property Report" to include in listings
- MLS integration: "This home has a ZAFTO Performance Index of 91 with full service documentation"
- Home inspection supplement: inspector + ZAFTO record = comprehensive picture
- Title company integration: transfer happens as part of closing workflow

**Why this is a moat:** A buyer who inherits 15 years of detailed property records on ZAFTO will never switch to a competitor platform. The data is irreplaceable. And when THEY sell in 10 years, they transfer an even richer record. The platform gets stickier with every transaction.

---

### Feature 13: DIY Guidance with Contractor Guardrails

**What it is:** AI-generated instructions for simple maintenance tasks, personalized to the exact equipment in the homeowner's profile â€” with clear boundaries on when to call a professional.

**Example:**

```
â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”
â”‚  HOW TO: Change Your Furnace Filter                 â”‚
â”‚  Personalized for YOUR system                       â”‚
â”‚                                                     â”‚
â”‚  Your furnace: Carrier 59TP6                        â”‚
â”‚  Filter size: 20x25x4 MERV-11                      â”‚
â”‚  Filter location: Right side panel, bottom          â”‚
â”‚                                                     â”‚
â”‚  Steps:                                             â”‚
â”‚  1. Turn off furnace at thermostat                  â”‚
â”‚  2. Locate filter compartment (right side, bottom)  â”‚
â”‚  3. Slide out old filter â€” note arrow direction     â”‚
â”‚  4. Insert new filter with arrow pointing toward    â”‚
â”‚     furnace (toward blower)                         â”‚
â”‚  5. Close compartment, turn furnace back on         â”‚
â”‚                                                     â”‚
â”‚  â± Time: 5 minutes | ðŸ’° Filter cost: ~$18-25      â”‚
â”‚                                                     â”‚
â”‚  âš ï¸ CALL A PRO IF:                                  â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Filter is black/severely clogged (airflow issue) â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ You hear unusual noises after replacing          â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Furnace doesn't restart properly                 â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ You notice soot or burn marks on/near filter     â”‚
â”‚  [Request Inspection from Preferred Contractor]     â”‚
â”‚                                                     â”‚
â”‚  [Mark Filter Changed]  [Set Next Reminder: 90 days]â”‚
â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜
```

**What AI covers (safe DIY):**
- Filter changes (HVAC, water, range hood)
- Thermostat adjustments and programming
- Garbage disposal resets
- Circuit breaker resets (tripped, not repeatedly tripping)
- Smoke/CO detector battery replacement and testing
- Outdoor faucet winterization
- Gutter inspection (ground-level visual only)
- Toilet flapper replacement
- Drain maintenance (baking soda + vinegar, NOT chemical)

**What AI NEVER covers (always call a pro):**
- Anything electrical beyond resetting a breaker
- Gas line anything
- Refrigerant handling
- Structural modifications
- Plumbing beyond basic fixture maintenance
- Roof work requiring ladder/height
- Anything requiring permits
- Anything involving asbestos, lead, mold assessment

**Contractor trust angle:** The AI actively DRIVES business to contractors. Every DIY guide includes "call a pro if" thresholds. Contractors see this as a feature, not a threat â€” it educates clients and catches the jobs that need professional attention. An informed homeowner who changed their own filter but calls about the weird noise is a BETTER client than one who ignores both.

---

| Tax Basis Tracker | â€” | Full access + export for tax preparer |
| Seasonal Maintenance Checklists | View checklist | Interactive, reminders, contractor integration, history |
| Multi-User Household Access | 1 additional user | Unlimited household members + roles |
| Transfer-with-Property | âœ… (data portability is a right, not a feature) | Enhanced report formatting for real estate |
| DIY Guidance | 3 guides/month | Unlimited + personalized to exact equipment |

### Implementation Complexity (Honest Assessment)

Most of these features are **data views on existing Firestore collections**, not new engineering challenges. The hard work is Firestore wiring (Sprint 2) and the AI service architecture (Doc 23). These features ride on top.

| Feature | Complexity | Why |
|---------|:----------:|-----|
| Emergency Home Profile | ðŸŸ¢ Low | Form + photos + offline cache. Simple CRUD. |
| Energy & Rebate Dashboard | ðŸŸ¡ Medium | External API integration (DSIRE database). Rebate data changes. |
| Tax Basis Tracker | ðŸŸ¢ Low | Filtered query on existing job records + classification flag. |
| Seasonal Checklists | ðŸŸ¢ Low | AI prompt + equipment data â†’ generated checklist. Template-driven. |
| Multi-User Household | ðŸŸ¡ Medium | Auth rules, permission model, invitation flow. Standard but needs care. |
| Transfer-with-Property | ðŸŸ¡ Medium | Data migration logic, selective transfer, access revocation. |
| DIY Guidance | ðŸŸ¢ Low | AI prompt + equipment context â†’ instructions. Content, not code. |

None of these are architectural nightmares. The nightmare would be building the underlying data layer from scratch â€” but that's already designed.

---

The moat only exists if the homeowner feels this belongs to THEM and gives them value they can't get anywhere else. These thirteen features make that real.

---

## APPENDIX E â€” REAL ESTATE INTEGRATION & PROPERTY CERTIFICATION
### Added: February 4, 2026

### The Strategic Question

Can a ZAFTO property record become an official, legally meaningful document in real estate transactions â€” one that justifies higher sale prices and becomes a standard part of buying and selling homes?

**Short answer:** Yes. But ZAFTO doesn't need to become a legal document itself. It needs to become **the thing that legal documents reference** â€” the authoritative source of property condition data that appraisers, inspectors, insurers, lenders, and agents all rely on. That's a more powerful position than being just another form in the closing packet.

---

### How Home Prices Are Actually Justified

Most homeowners think price is based on square footage and location. In reality, five parties influence the final transaction price, and ZAFTO can feed data to all five:

| Party | What They Do | Current Data Source | ZAFTO Advantage |
|-------|-------------|-------------------|-----------------|
| **Listing Agent** | Sets asking price based on comps + condition | CMA (comparative market analysis) + visual walkthrough | Full improvement history with costs, permits, equipment ages |
| **Appraiser** | Determines lender-approved value | Comps + 30-minute walkthrough + whatever seller mentions | Documented improvements with receipts â†’ defensible upward adjustments |
| **Home Inspector** | Reports condition to buyer | 3-hour visual inspection | Years of service data, equipment history, maintenance compliance |
| **Insurance Underwriter** | Sets premiums based on risk | Age of home + basic construction type + claims history | Equipment condition, maintenance record, risk alerts addressed, Performance Index |
| **Buyer** | Decides what they'll pay | Emotion + inspection report + agent advice | Complete property intelligence = confidence = willingness to pay asking price |

**The core insight:** Every one of these parties is currently making decisions with incomplete data. ZAFTO has better data than any of them. The platform that provides that data becomes indispensable.

---

### The ZAFTO Property Report

**What it is:** A professionally formatted, verifiable report generated from the property's ZAFTO record â€” designed specifically for real estate transactions.
